1 INTRODUCTION
This report contains the results of the emissions estimation of the Impact Study project
Environmental (EIA) “Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Concentrate Production
of Rare Earths”, hereinafter, “the Project”, considering particulate matter and gases, according to the
schedule of activities for the construction, operation and closure phase.
2 GENERAL BACKGROUND OF THE PROJECT
2.1 Description
The Project corresponds to the set of works and activities that will allow the construction and operation of
a mining site and a clay processing plant, a material present in the area, which by
natural effects is highly weathered, with the presence of lanthanides adsorbed in the
clay minerals.
The processing plant has a capacity to process up to 320 tons/hour of clays
humid and produce approximately 1,700 dry tons per year of Rare Earth concentrate, which
They are equivalent to around 3,100 wet tons of concentrate per year.
In addition to the above, the Project considers three (3) clay extraction zones (hereinafter “ZE) ZE
“Victoria Norte”, ZE “Luna”, ZE “Maite”, one (1) disposal area (hereinafter ZD) for ballast and clays
washed ZD “Neptuno”, one (1) vegetal soil collection area (hereinafter “ZAV”), a
clay processing (the Plant), a stockpile (stockpile) for the temporary collection of previous material and
after processing (when operating conditions due to weather do not allow the
direct operation from the ZE and towards the ZD), an electrical line and its connection to an existing line and the
construction of internal roads to access different areas. Furthermore, the modification is considered
of an existing section of approximately 1.22 km of the Hualpén – San Fernando pipeline, owned
of ENAP, reason for the exploitation of the Maite ZE. The project in turn has the implementation of
temporary works corresponding to work facilities, for the construction and enabling of the
Project works.
It is important to take into consideration that the ZE will be operated only with mobile equipment.
mechanized vehicles, such as hydraulic excavators, front loaders and dump trucks, since the
material of interest is found superficially, the above is explained by the origin of the type of soil
present in the project area, of the residual type, formed from natural weathering by
physical and chemical agents of the rock. As a result of the above, extraction does not require the use and/or
1
==================================================================================

==================================================================================

storage of explosives to carry out blasting nor are crushing processes considered
nor grinding of the material during processing in the plant.
2.2 Location
The parts, works and actions that make up the Project subject to evaluation through this EIA,
They are located in the commune of Penco and Concepción, province of Concepción, Biobío Region. Figure 2-1
shows the general location of the Project.

3 ESTIMATION OF PROJECT EMISSIONS
3.1 General equation for calculating emissions
The emissions estimation methodology consists of the use of emission factors (EF), level of
activity (NA) and correction factor (1-P, where P corresponds to the control efficiency) that are possible
to relate to estimate the emission (E) of a substance “i” according to the following equation:
𝐸 = 𝐹𝐸 ∙𝑁𝐴∙(1−𝑃)
𝑖 𝑖 𝑖
The emission factors used in this analysis correspond mostly to those
recommended by the following documents, which base their calculations on document AP-42 of the
USEPA. Sources other than the previous ones will be expressly indicated.
- Guide for the Estimation of Atmospheric Emissions in the Metropolitan Region, 2020, Seremi de
Environment Metropolitan Region. (RM Guide 2020)
- Methodological Guide for Atmospheric Emissions Inventory M11, SINCA 2011 Methodology,
Ambiosis S.A. (Guide M11)
- Compilation and Systematization Service of Air Emission Factors for the Service of
Environmental Assessment, 2015, B.S. Consultants. (BS Guide 2015)
- Manual for the Development of Atmospheric Emissions Inventories, 2017, Ministry of the Environment
Environment. (Emissions Manual 2017)
3.2 Activities or emission sources
This chapter presents the atmospheric emissions of particulate matter and gases generated
during the construction, operation and closure phase.
The emissions-generating activities for each stage of the Project are presented in Table 3-1.

3.3 Calculation of construction phase emissions
This section addresses the various construction activities necessary to carry out the works.
and parts of the Project, including the transportation of personnel, equipment, materials and supplies, required
for the construction phase. This phase includes individual functional tests of the
equipment and installations and the joint operation tests until verifying that all the works and
Parts of the Project comply with the respective operational ranges established in the specifications
is
of design.
The activities that will be carried out during the construction phase are the following:
• Implementation of the installation of tasks.
• Topographical layout and land preparation.
• Enabling access and internal roads of the project.
• Implementation of power line.
• Construction of the processing plant.
• Conditioning of the land in extraction areas.
• Transportation and collection of topsoil layer.
• Extraction of material for the project's own roads.
• Enabling Neptune disposal area.
• Demobilization of the construction site.

Since the emission factor for traffic on unpaved roads depends on the average weight
of
the fleet and the fines content, and that these values vary for each section and year, it has been determined
a differentiated emission factor. The details of the estimation of the average weight of the fleet are detailed below.
continued
i. Average fleet weight
The average weight of the fleet was estimated considering the total flow of the Construction Phase and the weights
average number of vehicles to be used. The calculated average weight corresponds to a weighted average
to the flow and distance of each type of vehicle, which is estimated according to the following expression.
Where:
𝑊: Average weight of the fleet that transits a certain path and chronological year, in [t].
𝑃̅𝑖: Average between the weight with and without load (in [t]), of the vehicle that makes a certain type of trip i.
𝑁𝑣𝑖: Number of trips of trip type i.
𝑁𝑣𝑗: Number of trips of trip type j.
𝑛: Number of trip types.

ii. Determination of flows by section
The level of activity related to the resuspension of dust due to vehicle traffic on roads is not
paved corresponds to the total kilometers traveled by the entire fleet on said roads during
a chronological year. The total kilometers traveled are obtained from the product of the length of the section to
travel and the vehicular flow considering a one-way trip and a return trip.
Figure 3-1. Location of project access routes - Construction phase.

during a chronological year. The total kilometers traveled per section are obtained from the product of the
length of the trip and the vehicular flow within the section according to the flows presented in Table 3-31.

3.3.8.2 Activity level
The level of activity related to vehicle combustion corresponds to the total kilometers traveled.
for each vehicle type during a chronological year. The total kilometers traveled are obtained from
product of the length of the sections to be traveled, both paved and unpaved, and the flow
vehicular.

3.3.9 Use of machinery
3.3.9.1 Emission factor
To estimate the emissions produced by the machinery, the methodology indicated in the
Chapter 6 “Combustion of off-road machinery” of the “Atmospheric Emissions Estimation Guide”
in the Metropolitan Region” (2020) from the Seremi de Medio Ambiente of the Metropolitan Region. Bliss
methodology is based on two documents, firstly, on the “Median Life, Annual Activity, and Load
Factor Values for Nonroad Engine Emissions Modeling” (EPA, 2002), which provides the general formula of
obtaining emissions, and secondly, in chapter 1.A.4 Non Road Mobile Machinery (EMEP/EEA,
2019b), which provides emission factors and parameters that are more up-to-date than those indicated by the EPA.
The general equation to estimate emissions is as follows:
𝐸 = ℎ×𝑃 ×(1+𝐹𝐷)×𝐹𝐶 ×𝑇𝐴𝐹 ×𝐹𝐸
𝑖,𝑗 𝑖 𝑖 𝑖 𝑖 𝐵𝑎𝑠𝑒 𝑖,𝑗
Where:
• 𝐸𝑖,𝑗: Emissions of pollutant j, from machinery i, in [g/year].
• ℎ𝑖: Hours of use of machinery i, in [h/year].
• 𝑃𝑖: Power of machinery type i, in [kW].
• 𝐹𝐷𝑖: Deterioration factor of machinery i, dimensionless.
• 𝐹𝐶𝑖: Load factor of machinery i, dimensionless.
• 𝑇𝐴𝐹𝑖: Transient adjustment factor of machinery i, dimensionless.
• 𝐹𝐸: Emission factor of pollutant j, of machinery i, in [g/kWh]
𝐵𝑎𝑠𝑒 i,j
In turn, the deterioration factor (DF) is given by the following expression.
𝐾
𝐹𝐷 = ×𝐹𝐷
𝑉𝑈 𝑉𝑈
where
• 𝐾: Age of the machinery (between 0 and useful life), in years.
• 𝑉𝑈: Useful life of the machinery, in years.
• 𝐹𝐷: Deterioration factor relative to the useful life of the machinery.
𝑉𝑈
For this calculation, the assumption has been made that the age of the machinery corresponds to the life
useful of this, so an 𝐹𝐷 equivalent to 𝐹𝐷 is used.
𝑉𝑈
The parameters to use (FD, VU, TAF, FE) are shown below. In particular, for the factor
Base i,j
load (FC), based on what is indicated in the Guide, considering a scenario
conservative, a value of
i
0.8 for all off-road machinery.

Since the emission factor for traffic on unpaved roads depends on the average weight
of the fleet and the content of fines, and that these values vary for each section and year, it has been determined
a differentiated emission factor. The details of the estimation of the average weight of the fleet are detailed below.
continued
i. Average fleet weight
The average weight of the fleet was estimated considering the total flow of the Operation Phase and the weights
average number of vehicles to be used. The calculated average weight corresponds to a weighted average
to the flow and distance of each type of vehicle, which is estimated according to the following expression.
Where:
𝑊: Average weight of the fleet that transits a certain path and chronological year, in [t].
𝑃̅𝑖: Average between the weight with and without load (in [t]), of the vehicle that makes a certain type of trip i.
𝑁𝑣𝑖: Number of trips of trip type i.
𝑁𝑣𝑗: Number of trips of trip type j.
𝑛: Number of trip types.

ii. Determination of flows by section
The level of activity related to the resuspension of dust due to vehicle traffic on roads is not
paved corresponds to the total kilometers traveled by the entire fleet on said roads during
a chronological year. The total kilometers traveled are obtained from the product of the length of the section to
travel and the vehicular flow considering a one-way trip and a return trip.
Figure 3-3. Location of unpaved sections - Operation phase.
Source: GAC.

the different destinations that are within its route. The sections defined in roads do not

iii. Activity level
The level of activity related to the resuspension of dust due to vehicle traffic on roads is not
paved corresponds to the total kilometers traveled by the fleet on the respective section
during a chronological year. The total kilometers traveled per section are obtained from the product of the
length of the trip and the vehicular flow within the section according to the flows presented in Table 3-87.
Below, in Table 3-88 and Table 3-89, the summary of the activity level by size and year is presented.
along with the average weight of the fleet.

3.4.7 Resuspension of dust due to vehicle traffic on paved roads
3.4.7.1 Emission factor
Vehicle traffic during the Operation Phase is associated with the transportation of personnel,
inputs and waste removal. The paved roads to be used by the project consider traffic
by public roads between the project and the respective suppliers or recipients as appropriate.

Yo. Determination of flows by section
The level of activity related to the resuspension of dust due to vehicle traffic on roads
paved corresponds to the total kilometers traveled by the entire fleet on said roads during
a chronological year. The total kilometers traveled are obtained from the product of the length of the sections
to travel and the vehicular flow considering a one-way trip and a return trip.

3.4.9 Use of machinery
3.4.9.1 Emission factor
To estimate the emissions produced by the machinery, the methodology indicated in the
Chapter 6 “Combustion of off-road machinery” of the “Atmospheric Emissions Estimation Guide”
in the Metropolitan Region” (2020) from the Seremi de Medio Ambiente of the Metropolitan Region. Bliss
methodology is based on two documents, firstly, on the “Median Life, Annual Activity, and Load
Factor Values for Nonroad Engine Emissions Modeling” (EPA, 2002), which provides the general formula of
obtaining emissions, and secondly, in chapter 1.A.4 Non Road Mobile Machinery (EMEP/EEA,
2019b), which provides emission factors and parameters that are more up-to-date than those indicated by the EPA.
The general equation to estimate emissions is as follows:
𝐸 = ℎ×𝑃 ×(1+𝐹𝐷)×𝐹𝐶 ×𝑇𝐴𝐹 ×𝐹𝐸
𝑖,𝑗 𝑖 𝑖 𝑖 𝑖 𝐵𝑎𝑠𝑒 𝑖,𝑗
Where:
• 𝐸𝑖,𝑗: Emissions of pollutant j, from machinery i, in [g/year].
• ℎ𝑖: Hours of use of machinery i, in [h/year].
• 𝑃𝑖: Power of machinery type i, in [kW].
• 𝐹𝐷𝑖: Deterioration factor of machinery i, dimensionless.
• 𝐹𝐶𝑖: Load factor of machinery i, dimensionless.
• 𝑇𝐴𝐹𝑖: Transient adjustment factor of machinery i, dimensionless.
• 𝐹𝐸: Emission factor of pollutant j, of machinery i, in [g/kWh]
𝐵𝑎𝑠𝑒 i,j
In turn, the deterioration factor (DF) is given by the following expression.
𝐾
𝐹𝐷 = ×𝐹𝐷
𝑉𝑈 𝑉𝑈
where
• 𝐾: Age of the machinery (between 0 and useful life), in years.
• 𝑉𝑈: Useful life of the machinery, in years.
• 𝐹𝐷: Deterioration factor relative to the useful life of the machinery.
𝑉𝑈
For this calculation, the assumption has been made that the age of the machinery corresponds to the life
useful of this, so an 𝐹𝐷 equivalent to 𝐹𝐷 is used.
𝑉𝑈
The parameters to use (FD, VU, TAF, FE) are shown below. In particular, for the factor
Base i,j
load (FC), based on what is indicated in the Guide, considering a conservative scenario, a value of
i
0.8 for all off-road machinery.

3.5.8 Use of machinery
3.5.8.1 Emission factor
To estimate the emissions produced by the machinery, the methodology indicated in the
Chapter 6 “Combustion of off-road machinery” of the “Atmospheric Emissions Estimation Guide”
in the Metropolitan Region” (2020) from the Seremi de Medio Ambiente of the Metropolitan Region. Bliss
methodology is based on two documents, firstly, on the “Median Life, Annual Activity, and Load
Factor Values for Nonroad Engine Emissions Modeling” (EPA, 2002), which provides the general formula of
obtaining emissions, and secondly, in chapter 1.A.4 Non Road Mobile Machinery (EMEP/EEA,
2019b), which provides emission factors and parameters that are more up-to-date than those indicated by the EPA.
The general equation to estimate emissions is as follows:
𝐸 = ℎ×𝑃 ×(1+𝐹𝐷)×𝐹𝐶 ×𝑇𝐴𝐹 ×𝐹𝐸
𝑖,𝑗 𝑖 𝑖 𝑖 𝑖 𝐵𝑎𝑠𝑒 𝑖,𝑗
Where:
• 𝐸𝑖,𝑗: Emissions of pollutant j, from machinery i, in [g/year].
• ℎ𝑖: Hours of use of machinery i, in [h/year].
• 𝑃𝑖: Power of machinery type i, in [kW].
• 𝐹𝐷𝑖: Deterioration factor of machinery i, dimensionless.
• 𝐹𝐶𝑖: Load factor of machinery i, dimensionless.
• 𝑇𝐴𝐹𝑖: Transient adjustment factor of machinery i, dimensionless.
• 𝐹𝐸: Emission factor of pollutant j, of machinery i, in [g/kWh]
𝐵𝑎𝑠𝑒 i,j
In turn, the deterioration factor (DF) is given by the following expression.
𝐾
𝐹𝐷 = ×𝐹𝐷
𝑉𝑈 𝑉𝑈
where
• 𝐾: Age of the machinery (between 0 and useful life), in years.
• 𝑉𝑈: Useful life of the machinery, in years.
• 𝐹𝐷: Deterioration factor relative to the useful life of the machinery.
𝑉𝑈
For this calculation, the assumption has been made that the age of the machinery corresponds to the life
useful of this, so an 𝐹𝐷 equivalent to 𝐹𝐷 is used.
𝑉𝑈
The parameters to use (FD, VU, TAF, FE) are shown below. In particular, for the factor
Base i,j
load (FC), based on what is indicated in the Guide, considering a conservative scenario, a value of
i
0.8 for all off-road machinery.

3.7 PPDA Compliance Verification (D.S 6/2018) MMA
3.7.1.1 Limits established in the PPDA
According to what was stated in the article
53 of the D.S. 6/2018 MMA, Prevention and Safety Plan
Atmospheric Decontamination for the communes of Concepción Metropolitano”:
“the projects or activities and their modifications that enter the Impact Evaluation System
(SEIA) that generate an increase in direct and/or indirect emissions with respect to their situation
base, in values equal to or greater than those presented in Table Nº27, must compensate their
emissions by 120% of the total annual amount of emissions from the activity or project.”

emission for each activity, which were obtained from the Database “GHG Emission Factors

5 CONCLUSIONS
From the emissions inventory carried out it can be concluded that:
During the construction phase of the Project, which has a duration of 24 months, emissions of
Particulate matter is generated mainly by vehicle traffic on unpaved roads.
paved, estimating maximum total annual emissions of 101 tons of PM30, 35.4
tons of PM10, and 11.5 tons of PM2.5 for year 1. Gas emissions are generated
mainly due to the use of machinery, estimating maximum total emissions during year 1 of
construction of 73.4 tons of NOx, 0.28 tons of SO₂, 51.7 tons of CO and 6.4 tons of
VOC.
In relation to the operation phase, the highest emissions occur during year 6 of the project,
where the main source of particulate matter corresponds mainly to vehicle traffic in
unpaved roads. The maximum estimated emissions are 383.3 tons of PM30, 110.3
tons of PM10 and 16.11 tons of PM2.5. As for gas emissions, the main source is
machinery combustion with total emissions of 27.7 tons of NOx, 41.9 tons of CO and 3.5
tons of NH3.
The closure phase has a duration of 12 months, the estimated emissions total 44.6 tons of
MP30, 14.05 tons of MP10, 3.9 tons of MP2.5, with respect to gaseous pollutants,
estimates a total of 28.5 tons of NOx, 10.9 tons of CO, 1.52 t/year of SO and 2.72 tons of
2
VOC.
Regarding greenhouse gas emissions for the entire project, it is estimated that they are
present a maximum of 16,852 tons of CO eq per year, which would be generated in year 7 of the
2
operation phase of the Project, mainly due to transportation activities. By way of
reference, it is known that during the year 2021, 6,305 kt of CO2 equivalent were generated (6,305,000
tons) as direct emissions
s from copper mining in Chile6.
Finally, it can be determined that the project exceeds the established maximum emissions limits.
in table No. 27 (DS6/2018 MMA), having to compensate 120% of its emissions in accordance with the
contents and considerations indicated in D.S.N°6/2018.
6 “GHG emissions in copper mining in 2021 and analysis of the current context” - Chilean Copper Commission.
